  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0f919925-56e3-4de6-944e-6c3562f4ca70'
      });

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/248283-is-the-narrator-sane-or-is-he-insane--">Is the narrator sane or is he insane??? ;-)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_248283'><a id="like_count_community_question_248283" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/248283?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F899492.The_Tell_Tale_Heart">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/248283-is-the-narrator-sane-or-is-he-insane--">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/248283-is-the-narrator-sane-or-is-he-insane--">See all 10 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43242370-sara"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1505784265i/43242370._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43242370-sara">Sara</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I believe he is insane trying to convince us he is sane.<br/>Many times he mentions that he isn't crazy because of one reason or another.<br/>"TRUE! --nervous -<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I believe he is insane trying to convince us he is sane.<br />Many times he mentions that he isn't crazy because of one reason or another.<br />"TRUE! --nervous --very, very dreadfully nervous I had been and am; but why will you say that I am mad? The disease had sharpened my senses --not destroyed --not dulled them. ... How, then, am I mad? Hearken! and observe how healthily --how calmly I can tell you the whole story."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1457244-did-anyone-else-think-this-was-a-bit">Did anyone else think this was a bit creepy? He stalked the poor man! WHY??</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1457244'><a id="like_count_community_question_1457244" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1457244?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F899492.The_Tell_Tale_Heart">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1457244-did-anyone-else-think-this-was-a-bit">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1457244-did-anyone-else-think-this-was-a-bit">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/93151745-gurmehar"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1549351839i/93151745._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/93151745-gurmehar">Gurmehar</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Reading the story, you will realise that the narrator has unbalanced thoughts. The story does not tell as to why does he want to kill the old man who <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Reading the story, you will realise that the narrator has unbalanced thoughts. The story does not tell as to why does he want to kill the old man who has striking blue 'vulture eyes'. It is the whole planning and strategising stage where he maps his steps for that one night where he would take charge and murder the old man. He did not stalk, as he was already in the same house as his caretaker, therefore, he kept an account of the old man's night routine and sleeping pattern. <br /><br />The story is definitely creepy and a little disturbing, but it is so well written by Edgar Allan Poe, especially with the use of unconventional language( use of expressions - ha! ha!) which makes it very real and visual. Unlike other stories, it was easy to visualise the thought process, uneasiness and the anxiety the narrator had. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18055720686893270349"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/899492.The_Tell_Tale_Heart' title='The Tell-Tale Heart by Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Tell-Tale Heart</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe' title='Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Edgar Allan Poe</a><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605997835i/30410358._SY540_.jpg' width='480' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>A perfect haunting short story that will allow you to examine madness and wickedness at the depths of the human soul. It's not a horror story. But a kind of psychological tale. Strange the story. Easy to read. Quick to finish. Really loved this first-person storytelling. It's beautiful writing, and a very intense story will make anyone ponder for a long time.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>And have I not told you that what you mistake for madness is but over-acuteness of the sense?</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>Good</i></span>

It's not a horror story. But a kind of psychological tale. Strange the story. Easy to read. Quick to finish. Really loved this first-person storytelling. It's beautiful writing, and a very intense story will make anyone ponder for a long time.<br><blockquote>
  <i>And have I not told you that what you mistake for madness is but over-acuteness of the sense?</i>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322375320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10395224680312039096"><b>The Tell-Tale Heart, Edgar Allan Poe</b><br/><br/>The Tell-Tale Heart by writer Edgar Allan Poe, first published in 1843. <br/><br/>It is relayed by an unnamed narrator who endeavors to convince the reader of his sanity while simultaneously describing a murder he committed. <br/><br/>The victim was an old man with a filmy "vulture-eye", as the narrator calls it. The narrator emphasizes the careful calculation of the murder, and he hides the body by dismembering it in the bathtub, and hiding it under the floorboards. Ultimately, </span>
  <span id="freeText10395224680312039096" style="display:none"><b>The Tell-Tale Heart, Edgar Allan Poe</b><br /><br />The Tell-Tale Heart by writer Edgar Allan Poe, first published in 1843. <br /><br />It is relayed by an unnamed narrator who endeavors to convince the reader of his sanity while simultaneously describing a murder he committed. <br /><br />The victim was an old man with a filmy "vulture-eye", as the narrator calls it. The narrator emphasizes the careful calculation of the murder, and he hides the body by dismembering it in the bathtub, and hiding it under the floorboards. Ultimately, the narrator's feelings of guilt, or a mental disturbance, result in him hearing a thumping sound, which he interprets as the dead man's beating heart.<br /><br />عنوانها: «قلب افشاگر»؛ «قلب خبرچین»؛ «قلب رازگو و داستانهای دیگر»؛ نویسنده: ادگار آلن پو؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه دسامبر سال 2007میلادی، بار دیگر ماه جولای سال 2011میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: قلب افشاگر؛ نویسنده: ادگار آلن پو؛ مترجم: محمد حاج کریمی؛ نشر تهران، کوله پشتی، 1388، در 84ص، شابک 9786005337716؛ موضوع داستان کودکان از نویسندگان امریکایی سده 19م<br /><br />عنوان: قلب خبرچین؛ نویسنده: ادگار آلن پو؛ مترجم: مهناز دقیق نیا، ای.بوک<br /><br />عنوان: قلب رازگو و داستانهای دیگر؛ مترجم: مسعود فرزام؛ تهران، جامی، 1389، در 288ص<br /><br />ادگار آلن پو، از بنیانگذاران گونه‌ های پلیسی، علمی‌ تخیلی و وحشت شمرده می‌شوند؛ راوی داستان فرد بی‌نام و مجنون است، که پیرمردی را بخاطر نفرت، از چشم لاشخور مانند او، با آرامش به قتل می‌رساند، و جسد او را در زیر تخته‌ های کف اتاق، پنهان، ولی احساس می‌کند، که ضربان قلب او را، که هر لحظه بلندتر می‌شود، می‌شنود؛ این صدا که او را به مرز دیوانگی کشانده، سبب می‌شود، تا خود را لو دهد؛<br /><br />از متن: میدانستم که با اولین صدا از خواب پریده است، و وحشتش مدام بیشتر و بیشتر میشود؛ مرگ پا به اتاقش گذاشته و سایه اش مردک را احاطه کرده بود؛ نه میتوانست مرا ببیند، نه بشنود. ولی میتوانست احساس کند که سر من داخل اتاق است؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 05/08/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="10395224680312039096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17805194945879393033">An unnamed narrator who is telling this story plots to kill an elderly man because he hates his horrible and scary "vulture eye"...<br/><br/>Enjoyable, atmospheric, fast and creepy read. Poe was a great storyteller!<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2031297575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2031297575" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65909643-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515603070p2/65909643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2031297575?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/65909643-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65909643-michael?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65909643-michael?shelf=unreliable-narrator">unreliable-narrator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2031297575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15670579143794979229">What a quick little stab of the macabre this tale is! It's a classic example of the unreliable narrator, who tries desperately to convince the reader of his sanity even as he stalks, kills, dismembers, and buries an old man for no other reason than that the man's eye "resembled that of a vulture." Of course the harder he tries to convince the reader of his sanity, the more insane you realize he is: "You should have seen how wisely I proceeded--with what caution--what what foresight--with what di</span>
  <span id="freeText15670579143794979229" style="display:none">What a quick little stab of the macabre this tale is! It's a classic example of the unreliable narrator, who tries desperately to convince the reader of his sanity even as he stalks, kills, dismembers, and buries an old man for no other reason than that the man's eye "resembled that of a vulture." Of course the harder he tries to convince the reader of his sanity, the more insane you realize he is: "You should have seen how wisely I proceeded--with what caution--what what foresight--with what dissimulation I went to work!" <br /><br />This tale is also interesting in its use of the Ancient Greek technique of beginning "in medias res"--or in the middle of things. There's no preamble, no setting of the scene. Here's how the story begins: "True!--nervous--very, very dreadfully nervous I had been and am; but why will you say that I am mad?" You immediately get the sense that the narrator is reacting to something or someone, perhaps an unnamed interlocutor who's just told him he's mad. Or perhaps he's simply arguing or contending with himself? With a narrator like this, you never know, which is why I love unreliable narrators. There's no stability, no objectivity--everything is a shifting sand of the mind.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15670579143794979229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254330537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6750484510650313100">"... it was not the old man who vexed me, but his Evil Eye."<br/><br/>The nervous narrator decides murder is the only way to rid himself of this horrible eye -- but he didn't plan for the old man's heart. <br/><br/> This is one of Edgar Allen Poe's most famous short stories, from 1843. The unreliable narrator tells about how he was undone by an old man's clouded, "vulture-like" eye and beating heart ... or was he?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429028606i/14518113._SX540_.jpg' width='320' height='213' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The unnamed narrator is talking to another person, presumably a psychiatrist or policeman, trying his </span>
  <span id="freeText6750484510650313100" style="display:none">"... it was not the old man who vexed me, but his Evil Eye."<br><br>The nervous narrator decides murder is the only way to rid himself of this horrible eye -- but he didn't plan for the old man's heart. <br><br> This is one of Edgar Allen Poe's most famous short stories, from 1843. The unreliable narrator tells about how he was undone by an old man's clouded, "vulture-like" eye and beating heart ... or was he?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429028606i/14518113._SX540_.jpg" width="320" height="213" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The unnamed narrator is talking to another person, presumably a psychiatrist or policeman, trying his best to convince the listener ... not that he didn't commit the crime, but that he is not insane. And the more he explains how his sanity is proved by how very carefully he acted, how deliberately and coolly, the creepier it gets. This is a great, brief portrait of obsession and paranoia.<br><br>Available free online many places, including <a href="http://xroads.virginia.edu/~hyper/POE/telltale.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572927414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4765599252391546712">Edgar Allan Poe’s very short story from 1843 still packs a punch.<br/><br/>A narrator of unknown age, gender, and relationship to an old man, defends their own sanity, as they explain how they planned his murder - a man who they say has never harmed them, and whose death would not profit them. Nor do we know if they’re talking to themself, a psychiatrist, God, the police, or unimagined readers, more than 150 years later. The only reason given for the killing taps into the sort of fears many of us have in </span>
  <span id="freeText4765599252391546712" style="display:none">Edgar Allan Poe’s very short story from 1843 still packs a punch.<br><br>A narrator of unknown age, gender, and relationship to an old man, defends their own sanity, as they explain how they planned his murder - a man who they say has never harmed them, and whose death would not profit them. Nor do we know if they’re talking to themself, a psychiatrist, God, the police, or unimagined readers, more than 150 years later. The only reason given for the killing taps into the sort of fears many of us have in childhood. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540469934i/26499223._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>An eye peeking through a door</i>. (<a href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/b00grsvq" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br>Murder is so easy!<br><br>But then guilt kicks in, ticks in.<br>A metaphor made flesh, in flesh. <br>Bloody brilliant..<br><br>I read this as I waited to donate my 71st pint of blood. A mystical and mundane substance, essential for life. It’s an easy way to save lives, for those who are able. Eligibility criteria change, so if you'd like to be a donor, but thought you couldn't be, it's worth checking. For those in the UK <a href="https://www.blood.co.uk/who-can-give-blood/?fbclid=IwAR38ukz-bk6BeBU93kMeN9IA2ixfQfcfw9Hsv8TeYric0wS_VxYEq7uWv0c" rel="nofollow noopener">click HERE</a>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540469934i/26499224._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>”Save a life. Give blood.”</i>. (<a href="https://www.thebestof.co.uk/local/cannock/events/feature/give-blood-1361870731.1586/" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br>You can read the story, free, <a href="https://americanenglish.state.gov/files/ae/resource_files/the_tell-tale_heart_0.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.<br><br>I read it in parallel with HP Lovecraft’s <b>Pickman’s Model</b> (see my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2572928001" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>), which also opens with an anonymous narrator declaring their sanity.</span>

<div id="review_1749144672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749144672" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749144672?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_756297943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756297943" />
    <a title="Bionic Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean"><img alt="Bionic Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586709362p2/19300421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756297943?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bionic Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bionic Jean" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean">Bionic Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6503494-the-tell-tale-heart-with-an-alternate-ending">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=read-authors-m-p">read-authors-m-p</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=ghost-horror-supernatural">ghost-horror-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=19th-century-ish">19th-century-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756297943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2659802610867726780"><b>The Tell-tale Heart</b>, written in 1842, is one of Poe's best known short stories, despite its brevity. It is a study of the psychology of guilt, madness and paranoia, which are themes present in many of Poe's other works. The author uses a favourite claustrophobic device of his - <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[the boarding or walling up of living or dead creatures. The narrator's guilt manifests itself by his being haunted by supernatural beating sounds emanating from the heart. It is unbearable to him, so as in </span></span>
  <span id="freeText2659802610867726780" style="display:none"><b>The Tell-tale Heart</b>, written in 1842, is one of Poe's best known short stories, despite its brevity. It is a study of the psychology of guilt, madness and paranoia, which are themes present in many of Poe's other works. The author uses a favourite claustrophobic device of his - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the boarding or walling up of living or dead creatures. The narrator's guilt manifests itself by his being haunted by supernatural beating sounds emanating from the heart. It is unbearable to him, so as in <i>"The Black Cat"</i>, he is bound to reveal his crime to the police. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The reader assumes that this is an hallucination, although the narrator insists that he is not insane, but suffering from an <i>"over-acuteness of the senses." </i> The very first word of the story, <i>"True!"</i>, is an admission of his guilt, as well as an assurance of reliability. Nevertheless this is another of Poe's tales where he employs a firsthand account by an unreliable narrator, and where the suspense is increased by uncertainty; the reader becomes more and more doubtful that they should believe in the accuracy of the account.<br /><br />It is a powerful and deeply unpleasant tale. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The narrator is obsessed by one eye of an old man he has killed, a clouded, pale, blue, <i>"vulture-like" </i>eye, (which is probably a cataract), insisting despite this that he loves the old man and only hates the eye. He is kind to the old man, and cites his precise plotting to kill him as proof of his sanity. He then carefully details how he murdered and dismembered the old man. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />We are not told any details, to increase the starkness and impact of the tale. Poe thus manipulates the reader to concentrate on the horrific actions, without employing much of his usual skill with imaginative use of language. In this it is atypical of his writing, although the short, sharp simple sentences are used to great effect. There have been several virtuoso performances by actors such as Joss Ackland and Vincent Price. It must be a gift to a talented actor who can bring their full range of nuances of expression to what is essentially a soliloquy by a madman.<br /><br />This tale is quite simply a masterpiece of horror. Judge by the final words,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i>"tear up the planks! - here, here! - it is the beating of his hideous heart!" </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="2659802610867726780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1406697395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6770662618090885191">A short story classic! <br/><br/>Poe had excellent timing in the pace for <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, setting it to the quickening beat of a increasingly nervous heart. (Don't you dare comment below about how "the heart" mentioned in the story is the victim's, not the narrator's!)<br/><br/>Countless future writers, especially tv writers needing to tie things up within a half hour, would use this story as a framework for how to wring a confession out of a perpetrator.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, this story might not capture the terrifie</span>
  <span id="freeText6770662618090885191" style="display:none">A short story classic! <br /><br />Poe had excellent timing in the pace for <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, setting it to the quickening beat of a increasingly nervous heart. (Don't you dare comment below about how "the heart" mentioned in the story is the victim's, not the narrator's!)<br /><br />Countless future writers, especially tv writers needing to tie things up within a half hour, would use this story as a framework for how to wring a confession out of a perpetrator.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this story might not capture the terrified hearts of readers as it once did, because today this sort of homicide is fairly common place. We've been there, done that and seen it a hundred times on the morning news. It's almost as if <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i> has become a valuable suggested template on what to do if you're annoyed by your roommate. <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6770662618090885191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2289509312?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff" href="/user/show/68159473-jeff">Jeff</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2289509312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7628352977262453602">I read this in English class about two days ago, and at that moment, I realized what true writing talent was.<br/><br/>It’s a beautiful story.<br/>Haunted story.<br/><br/>I’ve never read that much of Edgar Allen Poe’s work, but snaps for him, cause at the end, my whole class went speechless. <br/><br/>This is a story where at the beginning, you really know what the hell is bloody going on , but by the end, everything ties together.<br/>Everything. <br/><br/>A truly captivating story starring a madman.<br/>:)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1869093661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1869093661" />
    <a title="Mohsin Maqbool" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3332742-mohsin-maqbool"><img alt="Mohsin Maqbool" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373637583p2/3332742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1869093661?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohsin Maqbool" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohsin Maqbool" href="/user/show/3332742-mohsin-maqbool">Mohsin Maqbool</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1869093661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2027247666306127805"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754251i/21646194._SX540_.jpg' width='800' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>READING an Edgar Allan Poe story is like you were watching a macabre dance of death in a gothic theatre in the dead of night. Mr. Poe is a master of suspense – chilling suspense. He builds it up slowly – so slowly – that you start feeling scared and getting goosebumps all over your body. You can hear your heartbeat just like the narrator does in “The Tell-Tale Heart”. However, it is not his heartbeat that he is hearing but that of a sleeping old man into whose bedroom he creeps into. A situation</span>
  <span id="freeText2027247666306127805" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754251i/21646194._SX540_.jpg" width="800" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>READING an Edgar Allan Poe story is like you were watching a macabre dance of death in a gothic theatre in the dead of night. Mr. Poe is a master of suspense – chilling suspense. He builds it up slowly – so slowly – that you start feeling scared and getting goosebumps all over your body. You can hear your heartbeat just like the narrator does in “The Tell-Tale Heart”. However, it is not his heartbeat that he is hearing but that of a sleeping old man into whose bedroom he creeps into. A situation like this can make anybody urinate in his pyjamas out of fear. <br>But what if the heartbeat keeps growing louder by the second? Louder and louder and LOUDER! You feel like tearing at your ears so that you can’t hear it anymore. The agony is absolutely unbearable.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754251i/21646195._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Where would Gothic horror be without Edgar Allan Poe? Anywhere but Poe territory!</b><br><br>Read the following extract from the tale to get an idea of what Mr. Poe can do to the reader:<br>“No doubt I now grew very pale; –but I talked more fluently, and with a heightened voice. Yet the sound increased –and what could I do? It was a low, dull, quick sound –much such a sound as a watch makes when enveloped in cotton. I gasped for breath – and yet the officers heard it not. I talked more quickly –more vehemently; but the noise steadily increased. I arose and argued about trifles, in a high key and with violent gesticulations; but the noise steadily increased. Why would they not be gone? I paced the floor to and fro with heavy strides, as if excited to fury by the observations of the men – but the noise steadily increased. Oh God! What could I do? I foamed –I raved –I swore! I swung the chair upon which I had been sitting, and grated it upon the boards, but the noise arose over all and continually increased. It grew louder –louder –louder!”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754958i/21646268._SX540_.jpg" width="640" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>I spy an evil eye.</b><br><br>In “The Tell-Tale Heart”, the narrator describes about an old man whom he likes a lot but still<br>wants to murder him. But why murder somebody whom you like? Because the old man has a "vulture eye" that sends shivers down his spine. It could also be an allusion to an evil eye. So, naturally, anybody with an evil eye has to be destroyed.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754251i/21646196._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Spotlighting the evil eye through the ray of a lantern.</b><br> <br>“It is impossible to say how first the idea entered my brain; but once conceived, it haunted me day and night. Object there was none. Passion there was none. I loved the old man. He had never wronged me. He had never given me insult. For his gold I had no desire. I think it was his eye! Yes, it was this! He had the eye of a vulture –a pale blue eye, with a film over it. Whenever it fell upon me, my blood ran cold; and so by degrees – very gradually –I made up my mind to take the life of the old man, and thus rid myself of the eye forever.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483754251i/21646197._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The album cover of Alan Parson's Project's "Tales of Mystery and Imagination".</b><br><br>Will the narrator succeed in his nefarious plans? Or will he botch them up? Read the story to find out. Play The Alan Parson’s Project’s “The Tell-Tale Heart” from their debut album “Tales of Mystery and Imagination” (1976) while you are doing so to enhance the excitement. <br><br>Link to The Alan Parson's Project's "The Tell-Tale Heart":<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O5NN8fK1tXo">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O5NN8...</a> <br><br>There are some of the best film versions of Poe's dark tale, including an animated one which has been beautifully narrated by James Mason, in the following link. I hope you enjoy them like I did. <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://flashbak.com/the-best-versions-of-poes-tell-tale-heart-the-worlds-first-x-rated-cartoon-and-voices-of-horror-51975/">http://flashbak.com/the-best-versions...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2027247666306127805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590699915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1438423878216420261"><b>Oh this is a really creepy good one!.......<i>(listened to the audio this time)</i></b><p>An unnamed narrator is the nightly intruder that watches the old man sleep. He must put an end to the <b>evil</b> eye that <b>haunts</b> his days and visits his dreams. He must be so quiet as he sneaks into the black as pitch chamber.....night after night.....and then, a shriek! The deed is finally done, but.....the <b>nightmare</b> only begins.</p><p><b>THE TELL-TALE HEART</b> is <b>dark</b> and <b>spooky</b> with a GREAT ending! One of my <b>POE</b> favorites!</p></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3408637981114482980">Entertaining ~ Great World Building ~ Haunting ~ Original ~ Scary ~ Twisted ~ Unpredictable ~ Wonderful Characters<br/><br/>Poe's masterpiece of suspense and horror -- best way to describe it simply. Poe to me was at the top of his form here. The writing is so descriptive and just builds and builds in suspense as the narrator weaves his tale. It's creepy and fascinating as the narrator tells his story of paranoia and obsession; working to convince someone and the reader that he isn't crazy.<br/><br/>A true gem. I'v</span>
  <span id="freeText3408637981114482980" style="display:none">Entertaining ~ Great World Building ~ Haunting ~ Original ~ Scary ~ Twisted ~ Unpredictable ~ Wonderful Characters<br /><br />Poe's masterpiece of suspense and horror -- best way to describe it simply. Poe to me was at the top of his form here. The writing is so descriptive and just builds and builds in suspense as the narrator weaves his tale. It's creepy and fascinating as the narrator tells his story of paranoia and obsession; working to convince someone and the reader that he isn't crazy.<br /><br />A true gem. I've made it part of my annual October/Halloween reading for years. One of those works everyone should read at least once.</span>

  <span id="freeText4692065799017285260" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415904350i/11862424._SX540_.jpg" width="397.8" height="265.05" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>p, is for Poe</u>
</b><br><br><b>4 Stars</b><br><br><i> Now this is the point. You fancy me mad. Madmen know nothing. But you should have seen me. You should have seen how wisely I proceeded –with what caution –with what foresight –with what dissimulation I went to work!</i><br><br>I have read <i>A Tell-Tale Heart</i> half a dozen times in my life and at every re-reading I am struck anew with Poe’s genius, he is one of the few writers I have ever come across who can entirely foreshadow a novel (or in this case short story) and yet still evoke emotion from me as a reader. <br><br>This is a short story of a man, believing himself to be entirely sane, who excuses atrocious behavior in the name of ridding the world of "Evil". It is a story of a mind falling apart when guilt is foisted upon it. A story of humanity at its raw, throbbing core.<br><br>A must-read classic in my opinion. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428516772i/14438361._SY540_.jpg" width="327" height="463.8" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1973696807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8620904367190403894">“And have I not told you that what you mistake for madness is but over-acuteness of the sense?” <br/>― Edgar Allan Poe, The Tell-Tale Heart<br/><br/><br/><br/>One of the most unforgettable short stories. Scary as anything too even reading it today. I picked this book to do a report on in my college literature class.<br/><br/>I am sure most have read it but if not..do it now! A great little masterpiece and just writing this is making me want to read it all over again!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5364077-connie-g?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798296953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10694374529648545064">I love this short story unreliably narrated by a madman. The tension increases--as does the beating of the heart--as the narrator becomes more unstable. Even though I've read it multiple times over the years, I always marvel at how Poe constructed such a great story.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596588295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18289957581994305851">I've been wanting to read some Poe because he's weird and dark and goth and sort of punk rock for his time. This was a short and easy read. Some guy is totally cray but insists he is totally sane and is all like:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542412640ra/26609466.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It kind of reduces insanity to a caricature, but maybe that was the point? Who knows. I sure as hell don't. I couldn't even figure out WTH was meant about him sticking his head through the lantern or whatever that was all about. I just can't picture what was going on. I have this picture</span>
  <span id="freeText18289957581994305851" style="display:none">I've been wanting to read some Poe because he's weird and dark and goth and sort of punk rock for his time. This was a short and easy read. Some guy is totally cray but insists he is totally sane and is all like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542412640ra/26609466.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It kind of reduces insanity to a caricature, but maybe that was the point? Who knows. I sure as hell don't. I couldn't even figure out WTH was meant about him sticking his head through the lantern or whatever that was all about. I just can't picture what was going on. I have this picture of a disembodied head floating around.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542412640ra/26609467.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know I'm missing something because I'm so Classics Stupid™. Still, it was creepy, although dated. I guess that is what you get when you ... read classics. I have very low brow tastes in books, in case you hadn't figured that out by now.<br><br>Final word: Needs more creepy.</span>

<div id="review_3475296236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3475296236" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3475296236?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3475296236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4863961059215883273">This is a short story that is considered a classic. It was written almost two hundred years ago and it still holds up today. In this one, we get to see the actual act of a murder and the immediate affect it has on the murderer.<br/><br/>This was so good and I am amazed how intense it was for a short story. The author does a wonderful job with the mood and the descriptions. Even though we never actually learn the name of the main character I was immediately enthralled by him as he describes his intention o</span>
  <span id="freeText4863961059215883273" style="display:none">This is a short story that is considered a classic. It was written almost two hundred years ago and it still holds up today. In this one, we get to see the actual act of a murder and the immediate affect it has on the murderer.<br /><br />This was so good and I am amazed how intense it was for a short story. The author does a wonderful job with the mood and the descriptions. Even though we never actually learn the name of the main character I was immediately enthralled by him as he describes his intention of murder. This was so well done and it is not even the highlight of this short story. The highlight is the conclusion as it leaves the reader to ponder if the main character acts out because of guilt or is he unstable (he did commit murder so it really could be that). I enjoyed the ending so much even though I knew how it ended.<br /><br />This was required reading back in my English class in high school and I remember me wondering what the big deal was about this story. I just didn't get it back then as this short story is a big deal and I would recommend it to everyone.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4863961059215883273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2009295437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009295437" />
    <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello"><img alt="Michael Sorbello" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521124600p2/4307906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009295437?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sorbello" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello">Michael Sorbello</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28236185-the-tell-tale-heart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009295437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7952633963975870961">The scariest of Poe's horror stories in my opinion. Poe effectively showcases the classic symptoms and behaviors of paranoia-induced insanity, a symptom that many violent serial killers display. Poe also shows an impressive knowledge and understanding of a deranged criminal's mind in a time when not too much was known about human psychology. <br/><br/>The disturbed protagonist shows psychotic symptoms including fixation, obsessiveness, dehumanization and paranoia, leading him to do something utterly despi</span>
  <span id="freeText7952633963975870961" style="display:none">The scariest of Poe's horror stories in my opinion. Poe effectively showcases the classic symptoms and behaviors of paranoia-induced insanity, a symptom that many violent serial killers display. Poe also shows an impressive knowledge and understanding of a deranged criminal's mind in a time when not too much was known about human psychology. <br /><br />The disturbed protagonist shows psychotic symptoms including fixation, obsessiveness, dehumanization and paranoia, leading him to do something utterly despicable to an old man without any ulterior motives. He tries to justify his delusions by fixating on his victim's vulture-like eye, treating it as a separate entity from the old man so he doesn't have to experience the guilt of his terrible crime. His guilt eventually manifests in the sound of the old man's heart beating beneath his floorboards, driving him mad until he finally confesses to murdering and dismembering the old man for reasons he can't seem to properly explain.<br /><br />A disturbing look into the psychology of a severely troubled individual and an early study of criminal behavior.<br /><br />***<br /><br />My Social Media<br /><br />My Instagram Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/michael_sorbello/">https://www.instagram.com/michael_sor...</a><br /><br />My YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs1eOzsOqcz5ey5JjGSbg">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs...</a><br /><br />My Wattpad Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-Sorbello">https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-...</a><br /><br />My Twitter Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror">https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror</a><br /><br />My Facebook Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorbello.104">https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorb...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7952633963975870961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060790076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13303308350550306859">I first read this, like many others, in elementary school. I remember listening to the teacher explain it and how the concept intrigued me. I read it again a couple years ago. I just finished my third read. The more we read, the better it gets! Poe has this power with words I don't yet understand or have researched or tried yet to analyze. He takes all the senses you own from inside your head and makes you live inside the story. He has an amazing story-telling ability that gives excitement and p</span>
  <span id="freeText13303308350550306859" style="display:none">I first read this, like many others, in elementary school. I remember listening to the teacher explain it and how the concept intrigued me. I read it again a couple years ago. I just finished my third read. The more we read, the better it gets! Poe has this power with words I don't yet understand or have researched or tried yet to analyze. He takes all the senses you own from inside your head and makes you live inside the story. He has an amazing story-telling ability that gives excitement and pleasure as you read. He creeps you out with the reality and depth of this psychopath who thinks he has superhuman powers. <br /><br />Man. I just love Poe! Absolutely mind boggling and baffling. What unbelievable literary power!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13303308350550306859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2209446793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209446793" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wY8TEtuh6E8ErO23fJ/NqifJaPOxmYRTxzEHtWv6vFG34qYRhxxNcKIT3sQSjz2YBWUHp1ILf0mGv+o4EfNXIw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gt/iyHbSWx1rgB67HhpyUzUXWggBBCNznUtNCCR4mcj0slfLKm/+Is0/LchwCoJhF7s1XOKW2GncxaCFXnFyug==')})
  }
//]]>

It was initially rejected, along with four other stories, by The New Yorker, but was ultimately published in Harper\'s Magazine in September 1953. It was adapted for an episode of Alfred Hitchcock Presents and starred Barbara Bel Geddes. Originally broadcast on April 13, 1958, it was one of only 17 AHP episodes directed by Hitchcock himself. The story was subsequently adapted for Dahl\'s British TV series Tales of the Unexpected.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe">About Edgar Allan Poe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1454522972p3/4624490.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe">Edgar Allan Poe
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
20,391
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18065244870106224389">The name Poe brings to mind images of murderers and madmen, premature burials, and mysterious women who return from the dead. His works have been in print since 1827 and include such literary classics as <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, <i>The Raven</i>, and The Fall of the House of Usher. This versatile writer’s oeuvre includes short stories, poetry, a novel, a textbook, a book of scientific theory, and hundreds of</span>
  <span id="freeText18065244870106224389" style="display:none">The name Poe brings to mind images of murderers and madmen, premature burials, and mysterious women who return from the dead. His works have been in print since 1827 and include such literary classics as <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, <i>The Raven</i>, and The Fall of the House of Usher. This versatile writer’s oeuvre includes short stories, poetry, a novel, a textbook, a book of scientific theory, and hundreds of essays and book reviews. He is widely acknowledged as the inventor of the modern detective story and an innovator in the science fiction genre, but he made his living as America’s first great literary critic and theoretician. Poe’s reputation today rests primarily on his tales of terror as well as on his haunting lyric poetry.<br /><br />Just as the bizarre characters in Poe’s stories have captured the public imagination so too has Poe himself. He is seen as a morbid, mysterious figure lurking in the shadows of moonlit cemeteries or crumbling castles. This is the Poe of legend. But much of what we know about Poe is wrong, the product of a biography written by one of his enemies in an attempt to defame the author’s name.<br /><br />The real Poe was born to traveling actors in Boston on January 19, 1809. Edgar was the second of three children. His other brother William Henry Leonard Poe would also become a poet before his early death, and Poe’s sister Rosalie Poe would grow up to teach penmanship at a Richmond girls’ school. Within three years of Poe’s birth both of his parents had died, and he was taken in by the wealthy tobacco merchant John Allan and his wife Frances Valentine Allan in Richmond, Virginia while Poe’s siblings went to live with other families. Mr. Allan would rear Poe to be a businessman and a Virginia gentleman, but Poe had dreams of being a writer in emulation of his childhood hero the British poet Lord Byron. Early poetic verses found written in a young Poe’s handwriting on the backs of Allan’s ledger sheets reveal how little interest Poe had in the tobacco business.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_allan_poe">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_al...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18065244870106224389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/19034527-the-tell-tale-heart">Quotes from The Tell-Tale Heart</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I heard a slight groan, and I knew it was the groan of mortal terror. It was not a groan of pain or of grief --oh, no! --it was the low stifled sound that arises from the bottom of the soul when overcharged with awe. I knew the sound well. Many a night, just at midnight, when all the world slept, it has welled up from my own bosom, deepening, with its dreadful echo, the terrors that distracted me. I say I knew it well. I knew what the old man felt, and pitied him, although I chuckled at heart.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7135673-i-heard-a-slight-groan-and-i-knew-it-was">13 likes</a>
            </nobr>

          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
